You are to determine whether the given **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided **evidence**. The evidence consists of a collection of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific entity or concept, and each value is a numerical indicator (0 or 1) that may indicate the presence or absence of information related to the claim.

### Key Rules to Follow:
1. **Do not use external knowledge** (e.g., general knowledge, prior information, or real-world facts) to make judgments. Only use the provided evidence.
2. **Do not assume** that a value of 0 means "not true" or that a value of 1 means "true." The values are simply indicators of the presence or absence of information.
3. **Do not infer** the meaning of the values unless explicitly stated.
4. **Do not use** any prior knowledge about the claim's truth or falsity.
5. **Only use the provided evidence** to make your determination.

### Task Description:
You are to analyze the provided evidence and determine whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the following criteria:
- If the evidence directly supports the claim, then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
- If the evidence contradicts the claim or does not provide sufficient information to support it, then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

The claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED** by the provided evidence.

- There is no information in the evidence about the content of the tariff, its purpose, or who framed it.
- The claim is about a specific historical event and individual, which is not addressed by the provided data.

Iteration 3: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction

You are to determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a collection of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific entity or concept, and the value represents some form of data (e.g., a boolean, number, or string). The claim is a statement about a specific event, person, or object.

### Task Overview

- **Input Format**: A list of key-value pairs (dictionary-like structure) and a claim.
- **Task**: Analyze the evidence and determine if the claim is **supported** or **not supported** based on the evidence.
- **Key Considerations**:
  - The evidence may include multiple entries for the same or different entities.
  - The claim may reference specific details (e.g., a film, person, event, or object).
  - The evidence may not directly support or contradict the claim.
  - You must **reason through the evidence step by step** to determine whether the claim is substantiated or not.

### Example of a Claim and Evidence

**Claim**: "The 2017 British period crime drama film is about the 1967 Detroit riot which is also known as the 12th Street Riot. Will Poulter starred in this film."

**Evidence**:
- {'key': 'Detroit (film)', 'value': 0}
- {'key': 'Detroit (film)', 'value': 1}
- {'key': '1967 Detroit riot', 'value': 0}
- {'key': 'Will Poulter', 'value': 0}

**Output**: "The claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence."

### Reasoning Steps

1. **Identify the claim**: Determine what specific information the claim is asserting.
2. **Analyze the evidence**: Look for any direct or indirect support for the claim.
3. **Check for contradictions**: Are there any parts of the claim that are not supported by the evidence?
4. **Determine relevance**: Is the evidence relevant to the claim?
5. **Evaluate the strength of support**: Is the evidence sufficient to support the claim, or is it insufficient?

### Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations

- **Film and media**: Knowledge of film titles, directors, actors, and events.
- **Historical events**: Recognition of significant events and their associated names.
- **Personnel and roles**: Understanding of roles in films, music, or historical events.
- **Data interpretation**: Interpreting the values in the evidence (e.g., 0 or 1) as indicators of support or lack thereof.
- **Logical consistency**: Ensuring that the claim is logically consistent with the evidence.

### Generalizable Strategy

- **Use logical deduction**: If the claim is not directly supported by the evidence, it is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Use evidence to infer**: If the evidence contains relevant information that aligns with the claim, it is **SUPPORTED**.
- **Avoid assumptions**: Do not make assumptions about the meaning of values (e.g., 0 or 1) unless explicitly stated.

### Output Format

- **Verdict**: Either "SUPPORTED" or "NOT_SUPPORTED".
- **Reasoning**: A detailed explanation of how the evidence supports or contradicts the claim.

### Feedback

- **Correct**: If the verdict matches the expected result.
- **Incorrect**: If the verdict does not match the expected result, and the reasoning is not clear or incomplete.

Iteration 4: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction

You are to determine whether a given **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided **evidence**. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where:

- **key** represents a location or entity (e.g., "Bangkok Art and Culture Centre", "Siam Center", "National Stadium BTS Station")
- **value** represents a numerical score or flag (e.g., 0, 1, or 6)

### Task Overview

You are to analyze the provided evidence and determine if the **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the following criteria:

1. **Direct Evidence**: Is there any explicit or implicit evidence in the evidence set that directly supports or contradicts the claim?
2. **Logical Inference**: Can the claim be logically inferred from the evidence, or is it contradicted?
3. **Relevance**: Is the evidence relevant to the claim? Are the key-value pairs directly related to the claim's content?

### Example Analysis

#### Example 1:
- **Evidence**:  
  {'key': 'National Stadium BTS Station', 'value': 0}  
  {'key': 'Siam Center', 'value': 0}  
  {'key': 'Bangkok Art and Culture Centre', 'value': 6}  
- **Claim**: "Bangkok Art and Culture Centre is close to the skytrain halt which is near the shopping center in the Thai city of Bangkok."  
- **Analysis**:  
  - The evidence does not provide any direct information about proximity or location relative to other points.  
  - The value of 6 for "Bangkok Art and Culture Centre" does not indicate proximity to a skytrain halt or a shopping center.  
- **Conclusion**: The claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Generalizable Strategy

- If the claim is **directly supported** by the evidence (e.g., a key-value pair explicitly states a location and its relation to the claim), then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
- If the claim is **contradicted** or **not supported** by the evidence, then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the evidence is **incomplete** or **inconsistent**, the claim may be **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations

- The evidence includes **key-value pairs** that may refer to **locations**, **events**, **people**, or **works**.
- The **value** field is not always explicit, but it can indicate **relevance**, **importance**, or **association**.
- The **claim** may involve **specific details** (e.g., names, dates, types of events, or specific relationships).
- The **evidence** may be **incomplete**, **inconsistent**, or **ambiguous**, which can affect the support or rejection of the claim.

### Final Answer Format

You are to determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific piece of information (e.g., a person, event, location, or entity), and each value is a count or a flag indicating the presence or absence of that information.

### Key Rules to Follow:
1. **Do not use external knowledge**—only use the information provided in the evidence.
2. **Do not assume** any information not explicitly stated in the evidence.
3. **Only use the evidence provided** to make a determination.
4. **If the evidence is insufficient** to support the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
5. **If the evidence directly supports the claim**, the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
6. **If the claim is contradicted by the evidence**, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Example of a Claim and Evidence:
- **Claim**: "The hijacked plane rammed by Heather Penney had a crash in Pennsylvania."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Heather Penney', 'value': 1}`, `{'key': 'United Airlines Flight 93', 'value': 1}`

### Reasoning Process:
- Analyze each key-value pair in the evidence.
- Determine if the claim is directly supported, contradicted, or not addressed by the evidence.
- If the claim cannot be confirmed or denied based on the evidence, mark it as **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Task Description:
You are to evaluate the claim and provide a verdict (SUPPORTED or NOT_SUPPORTED) based solely on the evidence provided. Do not infer or assume any information not present in the evidence.

### Feedback Guidelines:
- If the verdict is **SUPPORTED**, clearly state it in your final answer.
- If the verdict is **NOT_SUPPORTED**, clearly state it in your final answer.
- Ensure that your reasoning is clear and directly tied to the evidence provided.

You are to determine whether a given **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided **evidence**, which is a collection of key-value pairs. Each key represents a specific entity or concept, and the value indicates some attribute or relationship associated with it.

### Task Overview

- **Input Format**: The evidence is a dictionary-like structure containing keys and values. Each key represents a specific entity or concept (e.g., "Scotchausen", "Breakcore", "Supergrass", "Mike Smith (A&R man)", "Fall from the Ceiling", "Commissioner of the NBA", "Adam Silver", "J. Walter Kennedy", "1984 NBA draft"), and the value represents a numerical or categorical value (e.g., 0, 1, or other values).
- **Claim**: A statement about a specific entity or relationship.
- **Goal**: Determine if the **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the evidence.

### Reasoning Steps

1. **Identify the claim** and understand its core components.
2. **Analyze the evidence** to see if it directly supports or contradicts the claim.
3. **Check for relevance**: Does the evidence provide information about the claim's subject, its attributes, or its relationships?
4. **Look for contradictions**: If the evidence does not support the claim, or if it contradicts it, then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
5. **Conclude**: Based on the analysis, state whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Example of a Claim and Evidence

**Claim**: "Hardcore influenced the electronic dance music who made Scotch Hausen album."

**Evidence**:  
- `{'key': 'Scotchausen', 'value': 0}`  
- `{'key': 'Breakcore', 'value': 0}`

**Output**: `NOT_SUPPORTED`  
**Reasoning**: The evidence does not provide any information about the influence of hardcore on the music of Scotchausen, nor does it link Breakcore to the artist or their music.

### Important Notes

- The task relies on **domain-specific knowledge** (e.g., music genres, artists, and their influences) to interpret the evidence.
- The assistant must **reason through the evidence step-by-step**, not assume or infer information not present in the evidence.
- The assistant must **explicitly state** whether the claim is supported or not, based on the evidence, without making assumptions beyond the given data.

### Generalizable Strategy

- If the claim is about a specific entity (e.g., an artist, band, or person), check if the evidence includes any direct or indirect information about that entity.
- If the claim involves a relationship (e.g., "X influenced Y"), check if the evidence provides any evidence of such a relationship.
- If the claim is about a specific event or timeline, check if the evidence includes any relevant information about that event or timeline.

### Final Output Format

```
Verdict: [SUPPORTED/NOT_SUPPORTED]
Reasoning: [Detailed explanation of how the evidence supports or contradicts the claim]
```

The evidence consists of a collection of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific piece of information (e.g., "Chicken Fried", "Whatever It Is", "Ballarat Bitter"), and each value represents a numerical score or a specific attribute (e.g., 0, 1, 2, or a descriptive label).

### Task Overview:
- The claim will be about a specific song, show, beer, or other entity.
- The evidence will include a set of key-value pairs that may or may not relate to the claim.
- You must determine whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** (i.e., the evidence directly supports the claim) or **NOT_SUPPORTED** (i.e., the evidence does not support the claim).

### Key Considerations:
- The **values** in the evidence may represent numerical data (e.g., 0, 1, 2) or descriptive labels (e.g., "Chicken Fried", "Ballarat Bitter").
- The **keys** represent specific entities or attributes (e.g., "Chicken Fried", "Whatever It Is", "Ballarat Bitter").
- The claim may include specific details about the entity (e.g., genre, author, release date, etc.).
- The evidence may or may not include information that directly supports or contradicts the claim.

### Reasoning Process:
1. Identify the **claim** and the **evidence**.
2. Match the **claim** to the **evidence**.
3. Determine if the **evidence** directly supports the **claim**.
4. If the **evidence** includes specific details that match the claim, the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
5. If the **evidence** does not include the necessary details or contradicts the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Example:
**Claim**: "Whatever It Is" is a polka song by the Zac Brown Band, and is a follow-up to the band's number-one debut single, Chicken Fried which was cowritten by frontman Zac Brown and Wyatt Durrette, and was first recorded in 2003 for the 2004 album "Home Grown".  
**Evidence**: {'key': 'Whatever It Is', 'value': 2}, {'key': 'Chicken Fried', 'value': 0}  
**Output**: **NOT_SUPPORTED**  
*Reasoning*: The evidence does not provide any information about the song's genre, authorship, or release history.

### Generalizable Strategy:
- If the claim includes **specific, verifiable facts** and the evidence includes **directly relevant data** (e.g., genre, author, release date), then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
- If the claim includes **general or vague information** and the evidence does not provide **specific details** or **direct support**, then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Facts to Consider:
- **Music**: Genre (e.g., polka), artist, album, release date, etc.
- **Television**: Show name, co-creator, debut, etc.
- **Beer**: Brand, ABV, style, label features, etc.
- **Other Entities**: Person, event, product, etc.

### Final Output:
- **SUPPORTED** if the claim is directly verified by the evidence.
- **NOT_SUPPORTED** if the claim is not verified by the evidence or contradicted by it.

### Input Format  
The input consists of a list of dictionaries, where each dictionary has a `key` and a `value`. The `key` represents a concept or entity, and the `value` is an integer that may indicate a relationship, association, or frequency.  

### Task Description  
- **Claim**: A statement about an entity or event.  
- **Evidence**: A list of key-value pairs that may provide indirect or ambiguous information about the claim.  
- **Goal**: Determine if the claim is **SUPPORTED** (evidence directly supports the claim) or **NOT_SUPPORTED** (evidence contradicts or does not support the claim).  

### Key Considerations  
- **Ambiguity**: If the evidence is ambiguous or does not directly address the claim, the claim may be **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- **Common Knowledge**: If the claim is based on general knowledge (e.g., "Bellis is a plant"), and the evidence does not contradict this, the claim may be **SUPPORTED**.  
- **Specificity**: If the evidence lacks details about the specific event, person, or relationship mentioned in the claim, the claim may be **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  

### Example  
#### Input:  
```  
{'key': 'Chuck Versus the Role Models', 'value': 1}  
{'key': 'Swoosie Kurtz', 'value': 1}  
```

#### Output:  
**NOT_SUPPORTED**  
```  
### Reasoning:  
- The evidence shows that Swoosie Kurtz is associated with the show "Chuck" in some way (value 1), but it does not specify which episode or season she appeared in.  
- The claim specifies a particular episode (15 of the third season), which is not confirmed by the evidence.  
- The evidence is insufficient to support the specific claim.  
```  

### Additional Notes  
- The assistant should avoid making assumptions or using external knowledge unless it is directly supported by the evidence.  
- The assistant should clearly state the reasoning and the final verdict in the response.

- **Incomplete or ambiguous evidence**: If the evidence is insufficient to support the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

- **Do not assume** the truth or falsity of the claim based on external knowledge.

You are to determine whether a given **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided **evidence**. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific piece of information (e.g., film titles, album names, people, events, etc.), and each value represents a numerical score or indicator (e.g., 0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, etc.).

### Task Overview

- **Step 1:** Analyze the **claim** and break it down into its components.
- **Step 2:** Match each component of the claim to the corresponding **evidence**.
- **Step 3:** Evaluate whether the **evidence** directly supports or contradicts the claim.
- **Step 4:** If the evidence is insufficient to determine the claim's validity, mark the claim as **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Key Considerations

- The **evidence** does not contain any direct information about the claim's subject (e.g., no mention of the director of "West of Broadway" or the Grammy winner).
- The **claim** may involve **specific facts** (e.g., a film's release year, director's birth year, or a musical's title) that are not present in the evidence.
- If the **evidence** is **incomplete**, **ambiguous**, or **inconsistent**, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the **evidence** **directly supports** the claim, then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.

### Generalizable Strategy

- If the **claim** is about a **specific person**, **film**, **album**, or **event**, and the **evidence** contains **no relevant information** about that person, film, album, or event, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the **claim** is about a **specific fact** (e.g., "The director of 'West of Broadway' was born before the director of 'Simon Birch'"), and the **evidence** contains **no information** about the directors or birth years, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the **evidence** is **incomplete**, **ambiguous**, or **inconsistent**, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the **evidence** is **directly relevant** to the claim and provides **clear support** or **contradiction**, the claim is **SUPPORTED**.

### Example of a Generalizable Strategy

- If the **claim** is about a **specific fact** (e.g., "The director of 'West of Broadway' was born before the director of 'Simon Birch'"), and the **evidence** contains **no information** about the directors or birth years, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the **evidence** contains **direct information** about the directors' birth years, and the claim is about their age relationship, then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.

### Final Answer

**SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** — based on whether the evidence directly supports or contradicts the claim.

### Key Rules to Follow:
1. **Do not use external knowledge** (e.g., general knowledge, prior information, or real-world facts) to make judgments. Only use the provided evidence.
2. **Do not assume** that a value of 0 means "not true" or that a value of 1 means "true." The values are simply indicators of the presence or absence of information.
3. **Do not infer** the meaning of the values unless explicitly stated.
4. **Do not use** any prior knowledge about the claim's truth or falsity.
5. **Only use the provided evidence** to make your determination.

### Task Description:

- If the evidence directly supports the claim, then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
- If the evidence contradicts the claim or does not provide sufficient information to support it, then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

- The claim is about a specific historical event and individual, which is not addressed by the provided data.

You are to determine whether a given **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided **evidence**. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific piece of information (e.g., film titles, album names, people, events, etc.), and each value represents a numerical score or indicator (e.g., 0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, etc.).

### Task Overview

- **Step 1:** Analyze the **claim** and break it down into its components.  
  - Identify the subject (e.g., person, event, object) and the specific facts or assertions made in the claim.  
  - For example, if the claim is "John Lennon was the lead singer of The Beatles," break it into: "John Lennon" and "The Beatles" and "lead singer."

- **Step 2:** Match each component of the claim to the corresponding **evidence**.  
  - Look for key-value pairs in the evidence that directly relate to the components of the claim.  
  - If a component is not present in the evidence, note that it is not addressed.

- **Step 3:** Evaluate whether the **evidence** directly supports or contradicts the claim.  
  - If the evidence directly supports the claim (e.g., "John Lennon was the lead singer of The Beatles" is confirmed by the evidence), then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.  
  - If the evidence contradicts the claim (e.g., "John Lennon was not the lead singer of The Beatles"), then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
  - If the evidence is **incomplete**, **ambiguous**, or **inconsistent**, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

- **Step 4:** If the evidence is insufficient to determine the claim's validity, mark the claim as **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Key Considerations

- The **evidence** does not contain any direct information about the claim's subject (e.g., no mention of the director of "West of Broadway" or the Grammy winner).  
- The **claim** may involve **specific facts** (e.g., a film's release year, director's birth year, or a musical's title) that are not present in the evidence.  
- If the **evidence** is **incomplete**, **ambiguous**, or **inconsistent**, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- If the **evidence** **directly supports** the claim, then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.

### Generalizable Strategy

- If the **claim** is about a **specific person**, **film**, **album**, or **event**, and the **evidence** contains **no relevant information** about that person, film, album, or event, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- If the **claim** is about a **specific fact** (e.g., "The director of 'West of Broadway' was born before the director of 'Simon Birch'"), and the **evidence** contains **no information** about the directors or birth years, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- If the **claim** involves **multiple components** (e.g., "John Lennon was the lead singer of The Beatles and the author of *Imagine*"), and the **evidence** addresses only one component, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED** unless all components are addressed.

### Example of a Generalizable Strategy

- If the **claim** is about a **specific person** and the **evidence** provides no information about that person, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- If the **claim** is about a **specific fact** and the **evidence** provides no information about that fact, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- If the **evidence** is **incomplete**, **ambiguous**, or **inconsistent**, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Final Answer

**SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** — based on whether the evidence directly supports or contradicts the claim.

1. **Do not use external knowledge** (e.g., general knowledge, prior information, or real-world facts) to make judgments. Only use the provided evidence.
2. **Do not assume** that a value of 0 means "not true" or that a value of 1 means "true." The values are simply indicators of the presence or absence of information.
3. **Do not infer** the meaning of the values unless explicitly stated.
4. **Do not use** any prior knowledge about the claim's truth or falsity.
5. **Only use the provided evidence** to make your determination.

### Task Description:
You are to analyze the provided evidence and determine whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the following criteria:
- If the evidence directly supports the claim, then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
- If the evidence contradicts the claim or does not provide sufficient information to support it, then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Example:
#### Input:

#### Output:

### Reasoning:
- The evidence shows that both "George Kuchar" and "Arthur Penn" have a value of 0.
- There is no information in the evidence about their birth dates.
- The claim is about a specific historical event and individual, which is not addressed by the provided data.

Iteration 46: Proposed new text for system_prompt: **New Instruction:**  
Determine whether the given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific entity (e.g., a show, a person, a film, a plant, etc.) and the value represents some metadata (e.g., ratings, popularity, classification, or other attributes).  

**Task Description:**  
- **Step 1:** Identify the key and value pairs in the evidence.  
- **Step 2:** Analyze the claim to determine if it makes specific assertions about the entities in the evidence.  
- **Step 3:** Check if the claim is directly supported by the evidence, including any implicit or explicit relationships between the entities.  
- **Step 4:** If the claim introduces new information or makes assertions not covered by the evidence, mark the claim as **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- **Step 5:** If the claim is fully consistent with the evidence or can be logically inferred from it, mark it as **SUPPORTED**.  

**Important Notes:**  
- The values in the evidence are likely metadata (e.g., ratings, classifications, or other attributes) and do **not** represent the actual content, scheduling, or relationships between entities.  
- The claim may reference entities not explicitly mentioned in the evidence, which would make the claim **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- If the claim is about a specific event, timeline, or relationship that is not addressed in the evidence, it is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  

**Example:**  
Evidence: {'key': 'Skatoony', 'value': 3}  
Claim: "Skatoony has reruns on Teletoon in Canada and was shown between midnight and 6:00 on the network that launched 24 April 2006."  
→ **NOT_SUPPORTED** (evidence does not provide information about reruns, Teletoon, or the launch date of the network).  

**Generalizable Strategy:**  
- Compare the claim against the evidence to check for direct or indirect support.  
- If the claim introduces new information not present in the evidence, it is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- If the claim is fully consistent with the evidence, it is **SUPPORTED**.

You are to determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where the keys represent entities (e.g., places, people, events) and the values represent numerical or categorical data. Your task is to analyze the evidence step-by-step and assess whether the claim is logically and factually consistent with the evidence.

### Key Points to Consider:
- **Identify entities** in the evidence (e.g., places, people, events).
- **Analyze relationships** between entities based on their values.
- **Determine if the claim** is directly supported or contradicted by the evidence.
- **Use logical reasoning** to evaluate the claim, not just rely on surface-level matches.

### Example of Input Format:
Evidence:  
{'key': 'Kete Krachi', 'value': 0}  
{'key': 'Krachi West District', 'value': 0}  
{'key': 'Kwadjokrom', 'value': 3}  

Claim: The town that is connected to Kwadjokrom is a town in the Volta region.

### Example of Output Format:
Final Answer: **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**

### Task Description:
Evaluate the claim based on the provided evidence. If the claim is directly supported by the evidence, mark it as **SUPPORTED**. If the evidence contradicts the claim or does not provide sufficient information, mark it as **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Additional Notes:
- Values can be numerical (e.g., counts, identifiers) or categorical (e.g., regions, countries).
- If the evidence is ambiguous or incomplete, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the claim is directly stated or implied by the evidence, it is **SUPPORTED**.
- Use **common knowledge** and **logical deduction** to assess the claim, not just match the evidence.

### Generalizable Strategy:
- If the claim is a **direct statement** about a specific entity, and the evidence supports it, then it is **SUPPORTED**.
- If the claim is a **general statement** or requires inference, and the evidence does not support it, then it is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the evidence is **incomplete** or **conflicting**, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

Iteration 48: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction

You are to determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific piece of information (e.g., a person, event, location, or entity), and each value is a count or a flag indicating the presence or absence of that information.

### Key Rules to Follow:
1. **Do not use external knowledge**—only use the information provided in the evidence.
2. **Do not assume** any information not explicitly stated in the evidence.
3. **Only use the evidence provided** to make a determination.
4. **If the evidence is insufficient** to support the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
5. **If the evidence directly supports the claim**, the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
6. **If the claim is contradicted by the evidence**, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Example of a Claim and Evidence:
- **Claim**: "The hijacked plane rammed by Heather Penney had a crash in Pennsylvania."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Heather Penney', 'value': 1}`, `{'key': 'United Airlines Flight 93', 'value': 1}`

### Reasoning Process:
- Analyze each key-value pair in the evidence.
- Determine if the claim is directly supported, contradicted, or not addressed by the evidence.
- If the claim cannot be confirmed or denied based on the evidence, mark it as **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Task Description:
You are to evaluate the claim and provide a verdict (SUPPORTED or NOT_SUPPORTED) based solely on the evidence provided. Do not infer or assume any information not present in the evidence.

### Feedback Guidelines:
- If the verdict is **SUPPORTED**, clearly state it in your final answer.
- If the verdict is **NOT_SUPPORTED**, clearly state it in your final answer.
- Ensure that your reasoning is clear and directly tied to the evidence provided.
```

### Niche and Domain-Specific Facts to Include in the Instruction:
- **Claim types**: The claim may involve historical events, fictional works, real-life individuals, or abstract concepts.
- **Evidence types**: The evidence may include counts (e.g., number of events, people, or books), flags (e.g., presence or absence of a fact), or specific identifiers (e.g., names, dates, locations).
- **Logical relationships**: The claim may involve comparisons (e.g., "A came after B"), inferences (e.g., "A is the author of B"), or contradictions (e.g., "A and B are both false").
- **Ambiguity in evidence**: The evidence may not directly address all parts of the claim, and some parts may be assumed or inferred.
- **Temporal and factual accuracy**: The claim may involve dates, events, or facts that are not explicitly confirmed or denied in the evidence.

### Generalizable Strategy:
- **Directly check for support**: If the claim is fully supported by the evidence (i.e., all parts of the claim are confirmed by the evidence), then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
- **Directly check for contradiction**: If the claim is contradicted by the evidence (i.e., at least one part of the claim is not supported), then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Insufficient evidence**: If the evidence is incomplete or does not address the claim at all, then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Example of a Claim and Evidence:
- **Claim**: "The book *The Catcher in the Rye* was written by J.D. Salinger and was published in 1951."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'J.D. Salinger', 'value': 1}`, `{'key': 'The Catcher in the Rye', 'value': 1}`, `{'key': '1951', 'value': 1}`

### Reasoning:
- All three pieces of evidence directly support the claim.
- The claim is fully confirmed by the evidence.
- Therefore, the claim is **SUPPORTED**.

### Feedback Guidelines:
- If the verdict is **SUPPORTED**, clearly state it in your final answer.
- If the verdict is **NOT_SUPPORTED**, clearly state it in your final answer.
- Ensure that your reasoning is clear and directly tied to the evidence provided.

You are to determine whether the given **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided **evidence**. The evidence consists of a collection of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific entity or concept, and each value is a numerical indicator (0 or 1) that may indicate the presence or absence of information related to the claim.

### Key Rules to Follow:
1. **Do not use external knowledge** (e.g., general knowledge, prior information, or real-world facts) to make judgments. Only use the provided evidence.
2. **Do not assume** that a value of 0 means "not true" or that a value of 1 means "true." The values are simply indicators of the presence or absence of information.
3. **Do not infer** the meaning of the values unless explicitly stated.
4. **Do not use** any prior knowledge about the claim's truth or falsity.
5. **Only use the provided evidence** to make your determination.

### Task Description:
You are to analyze the provided evidence and determine whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the following criteria:
- If the evidence directly supports the claim, then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
- If the evidence contradicts the claim or does not provide sufficient information to support it, then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Example:
#### Input:
Evidence: {'key': 'McKinley Tariff', 'value': 0}  
{'key': 'William McKinley', 'value': 0}  
Claim: "The McKinley Tariff was framed by the representative who was later assassinated in September 1901."

#### Output:
The claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED** by the provided evidence.

### Reasoning:
- The evidence shows that the "McKinley Tariff" and "William McKinley" have a value of 0.
- There is no information in the evidence about the content of the tariff, its purpose, or who framed it.
- The claim is about a specific historical event and individual, which is not addressed by the provided data.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Information to Include in the Instruction:
- **Key-value pairs**: The evidence consists of key-value pairs where each key is a specific entity or concept, and each value is a numerical indicator (0 or 1) indicating the presence or absence of information.
- **Numerical indicators**: The values (0 or 1) are not binary in meaning. A value of 0 indicates the absence of information, and a value of 1 indicates the presence of information.
- **No external knowledge**: The assistant must not use general knowledge or prior information about the claim's truth or falsity.
- **Direct relevance**: The claim must be directly supported by the evidence, or the evidence must contradict it.
- **Absence of information**: If the evidence does not provide any information about the claim's subject, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Incomplete or ambiguous evidence**: If the evidence is insufficient to support the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Generalizable Strategy:
- **Analyze the claim** and determine if it refers to a specific entity or concept.
- **Check the evidence** for direct support or contradiction.
- **Use only the provided evidence** to make a judgment.
- **Do not infer** the meaning of the values unless explicitly stated.
- **Do not assume** the truth or falsity of the claim based on external knowledge.

### Final Output Format:
```

Reasoning: [Detailed explanation based on the evidence]

- **Input Format**: The evidence is provided as a dictionary of key-value pairs. Each key is a string representing an entity, and each value is a number (e.g., 0, 1, 2) or a descriptive string (e.g., "Hurricane Irene", "Out of Time (album)").
- **Claim**: A statement that makes a specific claim about a particular entity or event.
- **Task**: Analyze the evidence and determine whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**. The reasoning must be based on the direct relationship between the evidence and the claim.

### Key Considerations:

- **Direct Evidence**: If the evidence directly supports the claim (e.g., a key-value pair explicitly states the claim is true), then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
- **No Direct Evidence**: If the evidence does not provide any information that supports the claim, or if the evidence contradicts it, then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Ambiguity or Lack of Context**: If the evidence is unclear, incomplete, or does not provide sufficient context to evaluate the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Numerical Values**: If the value is 0, 1, or 2, it may indicate a lack of information, absence of occurrence, or a specific category, but it must be interpreted in the context of the claim.

### Example:

#### Input:
Evidence:  
{'key': 'North Blenheim, New York', 'value': 2}  
{'key': 'Hurricane Irene', 'value': 0}  

Claim: North Blenheim, New York was destroyed by flooding caused by the Hurricane that landed in August 2011.

#### Output:
The claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence.

### Reasoning:
- The evidence shows:
  - A location **North Blenheim, New York** with a **value of 2**.
  - A **Hurricane Irene** with a **value of 0**.

- The values do not provide any direct information about the impact of Hurricane Irene on North Blenheim, New York.
- A **value of 0** for "Hurricane Irene" suggests that the hurricane did **not** occur or was not recorded in that location.
- There is **no evidence** that the hurricane landed in August 2011 or caused flooding in North Blenheim, New York.

### Conclusion:
The claim is **not supported** by the given evidence.

### Additional Notes:
- The assistant must avoid making assumptions beyond the provided evidence.
- If the claim is about a historical event, a person, or a specific entity, the evidence must directly relate to that entity or event to be supported.
- If the claim is about a fact that is not mentioned or contradicted in the evidence, it is **not supported**.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Information:

- **Numerical Values (0, 1, 2)**: These are not always definitive. For example:
  - A value of 0 may indicate the absence of information or a lack of occurrence.
  - A value of 1 may indicate the presence of information or a specific category.
  - A value of 2 may indicate a lack of information or a specific category, but it must be interpreted in the context of the claim.
- **Ambiguity in Evidence**: If the evidence is unclear or does not provide enough context to evaluate the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Direct vs. Indirect Evidence**: The claim must be **directly supported** by the evidence, not inferred or assumed.
- **Contextual Interpretation**: The assistant must interpret numerical values and descriptive strings in the context of the claim, not as absolute truths or falsehoods.
- **No External Knowledge**: The assistant must not use external knowledge or prior information to evaluate the claim, only the provided evidence.

### Generalizable Strategy:

1. **Check for Direct Evidence**: Does the evidence directly support the claim?
2. **Check for Contradiction or Lack of Evidence**: Does the evidence contradict the claim or lack information?
3. **Evaluate Ambiguity or Context**: Is the evidence unclear or incomplete?
4. **Interpret Numerical Values**: How should the values (0, 1, 2) be interpreted in the context of the claim?
5. **Conclude Based on Analysis**: Determine whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the above.

### Final Output Format:
- **Verdict**: **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**
- **Reasoning**: [Detailed explanation of how the evidence supports or contradicts the claim]
